## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and temperature affects material stiffness and strength through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with linearly softening modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Voce-type saturation: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Thermal softening exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic plus plastic contribution)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (polynomial hardening with linear thermal factor)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * (c3 - c4 * T) (Swift hardening with thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (thermally activated flow based on Zener-Hollomon)
- Nonlinear elastic with thermal expansion: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress accounting for thermal strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) representing decreasing elastic modulus or yield strength with temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) structure representing dislocation density saturation at large strains
- Power-law hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 representing work hardening in metals (Hollomon/Ludwik behavior)
- Multiplicative decomposition → Stress as product of strain-dependent term and temperature-dependent term, reflecting separable thermo-mechanical response
- Thermal strain offset → (epsilon - c*T) representing subtraction of thermal expansion strain from total strain before computing stress
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) representing thermally activated dislocation motion or diffusion processes
- Elastic-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2) representing distinct elastic and plastic regimes
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appearing as ratio or shifted form (c0 - T)/(c0 - c1) representing proximity to melting point

- Term 2: `71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)` (where 5.003/8.314 ≈ 0.6018)
- Term 3: `3.305*epsilon**3*T - 3.305*370.17*epsilon**3`

Combining terms 1 and 3:
`(2.097 - 3.305*370.17)*epsilon**3 + 3.305*T*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`
= `-1221.4*epsilon**3 + 3.305*T*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`

So GT = `3.305*T*epsilon**3 - 1221.4*epsilon**3 + 71.356*epsilon**0.2*exp(-0.6018/T)`

The key structural features are:
1. `T*epsilon**3` term (from expanding `(c1+epsilon)**3` with c1=0, this gives `T*epsilon**3`)
2. `epsilon**3` constant term
3. `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-0.6018/T)` - this is the hardest part to match

The exponential term `exp(-c/T)` is crucial. Let me check which candidates have structures that could produce this.

**Candidate 48:** `T*c0/(T*c1 + c2) + c3*(c4 + epsilon)**4 + c5*epsilon**(1/5) + c6*epsilon**c7 + c8/(T*c1 + c2)`

This has `epsilon**c7` which is a free exponent - could give `epsilon**3`. And `T*c0/(T*c1+c2) + c8/(T*c1+c2)` = `(c0*T + c8)/(c1*T + c2)`. But we need `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-c/T)`, which this can't provide. The rational function in T can't replicate the exponential.

None of the candidates have `exp(-c/T)` or `exp(c/T)` type terms. The exponential terms present are:
- `exp(c*epsilon)` in candidates 7, 9, 11, 25, 26
- `sin(T*c + c)` in candidates 27, 35, 49
- Rational functions in T like `1/(T*c + c)` or `1/sqrt(T+c)`

The term `exp(-0.6018/T)` cannot be represented by any of these structures. For small values of the argument, `exp(-0.6018/T)` could potentially be approximated, but we need **exact** mathematical equivalence, not approximation.

Let me reconsider: could `exp(-0.6018/T)` be rewritten? No standard algebraic identity converts this to a rational function, polynomial, sqrt, sin, or `exp(c*epsilon)`.

**Candidate 48** has `epsilon**c7` with free exponent, but the T-dependence issue remains. The `T/(T*c1+c2)` term is rational in T, not exponential.

No candidate has both:
- A term proportional to `T*epsilon**3` (achievable via `T*(epsilon+c)**3` with c=0, or `T*epsilon` type terms with higher powers)
- A term with `exp(-const/T)` behavior

Since the GT contains `exp(-c/T)` and no candidate formula has this functional form (they have `exp(c*epsilon)`, rational functions in T, `sin`, `sqrt`, `log`, etc., but never `exp(1/T)` or `exp(-1/T)`), no candidate can be exactly equivalent to the GT.
